Kaluza-Klein with varying scalar field


unit coordinate convention: $dx^0 = c dt$

${c} = {{{299792458}} \cdot {{{\frac{1}{s}}{({m})}}}}$ = 1 = speed of light
${G} = {{{6.67384\cdot{10^{-11}}}} \cdot {{\frac{{m}^{3}}{{{kg}} \cdot {{{s}^{2}}}}}}}$ = 1 = gravitational constant
${{k_e}} = {{{8987551787.3682}} {{kg}} \cdot {{{m}^{3}}} {{\frac{1}{{s}^{2}}}} {{\frac{1}{{C}^{2}}}}}$ = 1 = Coulomb's constant
${\sqrt{{\frac{1}{G}}{({{k_e}})}}} = {{{\frac{1}{C}}{({{{11604670337.432}} {{kg}}})}} = {1}}$ = conversion from kg to C
${kg} = {{{8.6172202304994\cdot{10^{-11}}}} {{C}}}$
${ A}_u$ = electromagnetic four-potential, in units $\frac{{{kg}} \cdot {{m}}}{{{C}} {{s}}}$
${{ A}_5} = {1}$ in natural units, but to cancel the units of $\phi_K$ it is in units of $\frac{{{kg}} \cdot {{m}}}{{{C}} {{s}}}$ so $A_5 = c \sqrt{\frac{k_e}{G}} = $ ${{3.4789926447386\cdot{10^{18}}}} {{m}} {{kg}} \cdot {{\frac{1}{s}}} {{\frac{1}{C}}}$

${\phi_K}$ = scalar field, in units $\frac{{{C}} {{s}}}{{{kg}} \cdot {{m}}}$

${{ g}_{\mu}}_{\nu}$ = 4D metric tensor, with units $[g_{\mu\nu}] = 1$
${{ g}^{\mu}}^{\nu}$ = 4D metric inverse

${{ \tilde{g}}_a}_b$ = 5D metric tensor, with units $[\tilde{g}_{ab}] = 1$
${{{ \tilde{g}}_a}_b} = {\overset{a\downarrow b\rightarrow}{\left[\begin{matrix} {{ \tilde{g}}_{\alpha}}_{\beta} & {{ \tilde{g}}_{\alpha}}_5 \\ {{ \tilde{g}}_5}_{\beta} & {{ \tilde{g}}_5}_5\end{matrix}\right]}}$
${{{ \tilde{g}}_a}_b} = {\overset{a\downarrow b\rightarrow}{\left[\begin{matrix} {{{ g}_{\alpha}}_{\beta}} + {{{{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}}}} {{{ A}_{\beta}}}} & {{{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}}}} {{{ A}_5}} \\ {{{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_{\beta}}}}} {{{ A}_5}} & {{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{{ A}_5}^{2}}}\end{matrix}\right]}}$


What if we require a unit 5-velocity?
${{{{{ \tilde{g}}_a}_b}} {{{ \dot{x}}^a}} {{{ \dot{x}}^b}}} = {-{1}}$
split off spacetime indexes
${{{{{{{{{ \tilde{g}}_{\alpha}}_{\beta}}} {{{ \dot{x}}^{\alpha}}}}} {{{ \dot{x}}^{\beta}}}} + {{{{{{{2}} {{{{ \tilde{g}}_{\alpha}}_5}}}} {{{ \dot{x}}^{\alpha}}}}} {{{ \dot{x}}^5}}}} + {{{{{ \tilde{g}}_5}_5}} {{{{ \dot{x}}^5}^{2}}}}} = {-1}$
substitute definition of ${{ \tilde{g}}_a}_b$
${{{{2}} {{{ A}_5}} {{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{ \dot{x}}^5}} {{{ \dot{x}}^{\alpha}}}} + {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{{ A}_5}^{2}}} {{{{ \dot{x}}^5}^{2}}}} + {{{{ \dot{x}}^{\beta}}} {{{ \dot{x}}^{\alpha}}} {{{{ g}_{\alpha}}_{\beta}}}} + {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{ \dot{x}}^{\beta}}} {{{ \dot{x}}^{\alpha}}}}} = {-{1}}$
solve quadratic for $A_5 \dot{x}^5$...
$ \dot{x}^5 = \frac{1}{A_5} ( -A_\mu \dot{x}^\mu \pm \sqrt{ (A_\mu \dot{x}^\mu)^2 - {\phi_K}^{-2} ( \dot{x}_\mu \dot{x}^\mu + 1) } )$

On a side note, later we are going to set $\dot{x}^5 = \frac{q}{m} \sqrt{\frac{k_e}{G}}$.
If we do this now then the solution of the quadratic looks like:
$\frac{q}{m} \sqrt{\frac{k_e}{G}} = \frac{1}{c} \sqrt{\frac{G}{k_e}} ( -A_\mu \dot{x}^\mu \pm \sqrt{ (A_\mu \dot{x}^\mu)^2 - {\phi_K}^{-2} ( \dot{x}_\mu \dot{x}^\mu + 1) } )$
$\frac{q}{m} = \frac{1}{c} \frac{G}{k_e} ( -A_\mu \dot{x}^\mu \pm \sqrt{ (A_\mu \dot{x}^\mu)^2 - {\phi_K}^{-2} ( \dot{x}_\mu \dot{x}^\mu + 1) } )$

Let's look at the magnitude of this for some real-world values.
Electrons in a copper wire (from my 'magnetic field from a boosted charge' worksheet).
$I = 1.89 A =$ current in wire.
$\lambda = 7223 \frac{C}{m} =$ charge density per unit meter in wire.
$v = \frac{I}{\lambda} = 2.625 \cdot 10^{-5} \frac{m}{s} =$ mean velocity of electrons in wire.
$\beta = \frac{v}{c} = 8.756735364191964 \cdot 10^{-14} = $ unitless, spatial component of 4-velocity.
$\gamma = 1 / \sqrt{1 - \beta^2} = 1 + 2.959179033 \cdot 10^{-7} = $ Lorentz factor.
$\dot{x}^0 = \gamma, \dot{x}^1 = \beta \gamma, \dot{x}^2 = \dot{x}^3 = 0$ = our 4-velocity components, such that $\eta_{\mu\nu} \dot{x}^\mu \dot{x}^\nu = -1$.
$r = 0.1 m = $ distance from the wire we are measuring fields.
$A_5 = c \sqrt{\frac{k_e}{G}} = 3.4789926447386 \cdot 10^{18} \frac{kg \cdot m}{C \cdot s} =$ fifth component of electromagnetic potential, as stated above.
$\phi_q = \frac{1}{2} \lambda k_e ln ( \frac{r}{r_0} ) =$ electric potential ... but what is $r_0$? The EM potential has a constant which does not influence 4D or 3D EM, but will influence 5D EM.
Let's look at the potential with and without the constant: $\phi_q = \phi'_q + \phi''_q$.
$\phi'_q = \frac{1}{2} \lambda k_e ln(r) = -7.47382142321859 \cdot 10^{14} \frac{kg \cdot m^2}{C \cdot s^2}$.
$\phi''_q = \frac{1}{2} \lambda k_e ln(r_0) = $ arbitrary.
$A_i = 0 = $ magnetic vector potential.
So $A_\mu \dot{x}^\mu = A_0 \dot{x}^0 = \frac{1}{c} \phi_q \gamma = -2492999.2 \frac{kg \cdot m}{C \cdot s} + \frac{1}{c} \phi''_q \gamma$.
And $\frac{1}{A_5} A_\mu \dot{x}^\mu = -7.165865159852 \cdot 10^{-13} + \frac{1}{c A_5} \phi''_q \gamma$

Assume $\dot{x}_\mu \dot{x}^\mu = -1$.
$\dot{x}^5 = -2 \frac{1}{A_5} A_\mu \dot{x}^\mu = 1.4331730319704 \cdot 10^{-12} - \frac{1}{c A_5} \gamma \phi''_q$
Below in the geodesic equation, for the Lorentz force equation to arise we muse set $\dot{x}^5 = \frac{q}{m} \sqrt{\frac{k_e}{G}}$.
Let's insert this into the $\dot{x}^5$ equation above and solve to find what $\phi''_q$ would be:
$\frac{1}{c A_5} \gamma \phi''_q = \frac{q}{m} \sqrt{\frac{k_e}{G}}$
$\phi''_q = c^2 \frac{q}{\gamma m} \frac{k_e}{G} = c^2 \frac{q}{m} \frac{k_e}{G} \sqrt{1 - \beta^2}$
For an electron this comes out to be $\dot{x}^5 = \frac{q}{m} \sqrt{\frac{k_e}{G}} = 2.0410525849546 \cdot 10^{21} = 6.118921713508 \cdot 10^{29} \frac{m}{s}$.
$\phi''_q = 2.1287683635025 \cdot 10^{48} \frac{kg \cdot m^2}{C \cdot s^2}$
...which is a few orders of magnitude higher than what contributes to the EM field.

So, assuming we want our 5-velocity to be normalized with the 5-metric, and assuming our 4-velocity is normalized with the 4-metric, then it looks like the 5th velocity is made up of two parts:
1) the EM potential, dot the negligible 4-vel, which is on the order of $10^{-12}$ for our current through a copper wire.
2) the the arbitrary constant, which must relate to the charge-mass ratio, which is on the order of $10^{21}$.
Also notice that this shows then the charge-mass ratio in the Lorentz force law will be influenced by the 3-velocity.
Of course you can avoid the constraint that that charge-mass ratio is dependent on the 3-velocity if you just relax the constraint of $\dot{x}_\mu \dot{x}^\mu = -1$. Then, for constaint $\dot{x}^5 = \frac{q}{m} \sqrt{\frac{k_e}{G}}$, any deviations in the electric potential $A_t$ would relate to deviations in the 4-vel-norm (or in deviations in the Kaluza field, which I am keeping constant in this worksheet).




What is $\dot{x}_5$ in terms of $\dot{x}^5$?
${{ \dot{x}}_5} = {{{{{ \tilde{g}}_5}_a}} {{{ \dot{x}}^a}}}$
${{ \dot{x}}_5} = {{{{{{ \tilde{g}}_5}_{\beta}}} {{{ \dot{x}}^{\beta}}}} + {{{{{ \tilde{g}}_5}_5}} {{{ \dot{x}}^5}}}}$
substitute definition of ${{ \tilde{g}}_a}_b$
${{ \dot{x}}_5} = {{{{{{{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_{\beta}}}}} {{{ A}_5}}}} {{{ \dot{x}}^{\beta}}}} + {{{{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{{ A}_5}^{2}}}}} {{{ \dot{x}}^5}}}}$


${{ \tilde{g}}^u}^v$ = 5D metric inverse
Notice, if you see a raised 4-index, it is being raised by the 4-metric and not the 5-metric.
${{{ \tilde{g}}^a}^b} = {\overset{a\downarrow b\rightarrow}{\left[\begin{matrix} {{ g}^{\alpha}}^{\beta} & \frac{-{{ A}^{\alpha}}}{{ A}_5} \\ \frac{-{{ A}^{\beta}}}{{ A}_5} & {{({{{{{ A}_{\mu}}} {{{ A}^{\mu}}}} + {{{\phi_K}}^{-2}}})}} {{{{ A}_5}^{-2}}}\end{matrix}\right]}}$

${{{{{{ \tilde{g}}_a}_c}} {{{{ \tilde{g}}^c}^b}}} = {\overset{a\downarrow b\rightarrow}{\left[\begin{matrix} {{{{ \delta}_{\alpha}}^{\beta}} - {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}^{\beta}}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}}}} + {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{ A}^{\beta}}}} & \frac{-{({{{{ A}_{\alpha}} - {{ A}_{\alpha}}} + {{{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}^{\delta}}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{ A}_{\delta}}}} - {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}^{\delta}}} {{{ A}_{\delta}}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}}}}})}}{{ A}_5} \\ -{{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_5}} {{({{{ A}^{\beta}} - {{ A}^{\beta}}})}}} & {{1} - {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}^{\delta}}} {{{ A}_{\delta}}}}} + {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}^{\delta}}} {{{ A}_{\delta}}}}\end{matrix}\right]}}} = {\overset{a\downarrow b\rightarrow}{\left[\begin{matrix} {{ \delta}_{\alpha}}^{\beta} & 0 \\ 0 & 1\end{matrix}\right]}}$

The cylindrical constraint is
${{{{ \tilde{g}}_a}_b}_{,5}} = {0}$
Therefore
${\left[\begin{matrix} {{{{ g}_{\alpha}}_{\beta}}_{,5}} + {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{{ A}_{\alpha}}_{,5}}}} + {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{{ A}_{\beta}}_{,5}}}} + {{{2}} {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,5}}}} & {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{({{{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_5}} {{{{ A}_{\alpha}}_{,5}}}} + {{{2}} {{{ A}_5}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,5}}}} + {{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{{ A}_5}_{,5}}}}})}} \\ {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{({{{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_5}} {{{{ A}_{\beta}}_{,5}}}} + {{{2}} {{{ A}_5}} {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,5}}}} + {{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{{ A}_5}_{,5}}}}})}} & {{2}} {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_5}} {{({{{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{{ A}_5}_{,5}}}} + {{{{ A}_5}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,5}}}}})}}\end{matrix}\right]} = {0}$
Therefore, if $A_{5,5} = 0$ then we find:
${{ {\phi_K}}_{,5}} = {0}$
${{{ A}_{\mu}}_{,5}} = {0}$
${{{{ g}_{\alpha}}_{\beta}}_{,5}} = {0}$

metric partial:
${{{{ \tilde{g}}_a}_b}_{,c}} = {\overset{a\downarrow b\rightarrow}{\left[\begin{matrix} {{{{ g}_{\alpha}}_{\beta}}_{,c}} + {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{{ A}_{\alpha}}_{,c}}}} + {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{{ A}_{\beta}}_{,c}}}} + {{{2}} {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,c}}}} & {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{({{{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_5}} {{{{ A}_{\alpha}}_{,c}}}} + {{{2}} {{{ A}_5}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,c}}}} + {{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{{ A}_5}_{,c}}}}})}} \\ {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{({{{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_5}} {{{{ A}_{\beta}}_{,c}}}} + {{{2}} {{{ A}_5}} {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,c}}}} + {{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{{ A}_5}_{,c}}}}})}} & {{2}} {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_5}} {{({{{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{{ A}_5}_{,c}}}} + {{{{ A}_5}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,c}}}}})}}\end{matrix}\right]}}$
${{{{ \tilde{g}}_a}_b}_{,c}} = {\overset{c\downarrow[{a\downarrow b\rightarrow}]}{\left[\begin{matrix} \overset{a\downarrow b\rightarrow}{\left[\begin{matrix} {{{{ g}_{\alpha}}_{\beta}}_{,\gamma}} + {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{{ A}_{\beta}}_{,\gamma}}}} + {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{{ A}_{\alpha}}_{,\gamma}}}} + {{{2}} {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,\gamma}}}} & {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_5}} {{({{{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{{ A}_{\alpha}}_{,\gamma}}}} + {{{2}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,\gamma}}}}})}} \\ {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_5}} {{({{{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{{ A}_{\beta}}_{,\gamma}}}} + {{{2}} {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,\gamma}}}}})}} & {{2}} {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{{ A}_5}^{2}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,\gamma}}}\end{matrix}\right]} \\ \overset{a\downarrow b\rightarrow}{\left[\begin{matrix} 0 & 0 \\ 0 & 0\end{matrix}\right]}\end{matrix}\right]}}$

lower connection
${{{{ \tilde{\Gamma}}_a}_b}_c} = {\overset{a\downarrow[{b\downarrow c\rightarrow}]}{\left[\begin{matrix} \overset{b\downarrow c\rightarrow}{\left[\begin{matrix} {\frac{1}{2}}{({{{{{ g}_{\alpha}}_{\beta}}_{,\gamma}} + {{{{{ g}_{\alpha}}_{\gamma}}_{,\beta}} - ${{{{ \tilde{\Gamma}}_a}_b}_c} = {\overset{a\downarrow[{b\downarrow c\rightarrow}]}{\left[\begin{matrix} \overset{b\downarrow c\rightarrow}{\left[\begin{matrix} {\frac{1}{2}}{({{{{2}} {{{{{ \Gamma}_{\alpha}}_{\beta}}_{\gamma}}}} + {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{{ A}_{\beta}}_{,\gamma}}}} + {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{{ A}_{\gamma}}_{,\beta}}}} + {{{2}} {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{ A}_{\gamma}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,\beta}}}} + {{{{2}} {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,\gamma}}}} - {{{2}} {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{ A}_{\gamma}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,\alpha}}}}} + {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{{ F}_{\gamma}}_{\alpha}}}} + {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}_{\gamma}}} {{{{ F}_{\beta}}_{\alpha}}}}})} & {\frac{1}{2}}{({{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_5}} {{({{{{{2}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,\beta}}}} - {{{2}} {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,\alpha}}}}} + {{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{{ F}_{\beta}}_{\alpha}}}}})}}})} \\ {\frac{1}{2}}{({{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_5}} {{({{{{{2}} {{{ A}_{\alpha}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,\gamma}}}} - {{{2}} {{{ A}_{\gamma}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,\alpha}}}}} + {{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{{ F}_{\gamma}}_{\alpha}}}}})}}})} & -{{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{{ A}_5}^{2}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,\alpha}}}}\end{matrix}\right]} \\ \overset{b\downarrow c\rightarrow}{\left[\begin{matrix} {\frac{1}{2}}{({{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_5}} {{({{{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{{ A}_{\beta}}_{,\gamma}}}} + {{{2}} {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,\gamma}}}} + {{{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{{ A}_{\gamma}}_{,\beta}}}} + {{{2}} {{{ A}_{\gamma}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,\beta}}}}})}}})} & {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{{ A}_5}^{2}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,\beta}}} \\ {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{{ A}_5}^{2}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,\gamma}}} & 0\end{matrix}\right]}\end{matrix}\right]}}$

upper connection
${{{{ \tilde{\Gamma}}^a}_b}_c} = {{{\overset{a\downarrow e\rightarrow}{\left[\begin{matrix} {{ g}^{\alpha}}^{\epsilon} & \frac{-{{ A}^{\alpha}}}{{ A}_5} \\ \frac{-{{ A}^{\epsilon}}}{{ A}_5} & \frac{{1} + {{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{ A}^{\mu}}} {{{ A}_{\mu}}}}}{{{{{\phi_K}}^{2}}} {{{{ A}_5}^{2}}}}\end{matrix}\right]}}} {{\overset{e\downarrow[{b\downarrow c\rightarrow}]}{\left[\begin{matrix} \overset{b\downarrow c\rightarrow}{\left[\begin{matrix} {\frac{1}{2}}{({{{{2}} {{{{{ \Gamma}_{\epsilon}}_{\beta}}_{\gamma}}}} + {{{{2}} {{{\phi_K}}} \cdot {{{ A}_{\beta}}} {{{ A}_{\epsilon}}} {{{ {\phi_K}}_{,\gamma}}}} - ${{{{ \tilde{\Gamma}}^a}_b}_c} = {\overset{a\downarrow[{b\downarrow c\rightarrow}]}{\left[\begin{matrix} \left[\begin{matrix} {{{{{ g}^{\alpha}}^{\epsilon}}} {{{{{ Riemann curvature tensor:

using a specific stress-energy tensor:
$\tilde{T}_{ab} = c^2 \rho u_a u_b + P (\tilde{g}_{ab} + u_a u_b)$

${{{ \tilde{T}}_a}_b} = {{{{{{{{{c}^{2}}} {{\rho}}}} {{{ \dot{x}}_a}}}} {{{ \dot{x}}_b}}} + {{{P}} {{{{ \tilde{g}}_a}_b}}}}$
